Plume\nof Unsuppressed\nTakeoff\nCondition.\n\nVelocity\nTurbulent\nCoannular\n\nVelocities\nPlug\n\nNozzle\n\n(Axial\nwith\n\nComponents)\n180 \xc2\xb0\n\nShield\n\n97\n\nshearing of the baseline nozzle flow because of the presence of the\nshield flow. For X/Deq > 4 the turbulent velocities on the shield\nside are higher, with a maxim_nof 16.5%of Vmax at X/Deq ~ 7.\nThe asymmetryin the meanand turbulent velocities between the shielded\nand unshielded sides can also be noted from the sets of radial traverse data\nthat are presented in Figures 52 and 53, respectively.\nThe radial meanvelocity data in the pre-merged region (refer to data obtained at traverse J) indicate the distinct presence of the shield flow. At this location, the peak mean\nvelocity on the shield side is lower than that on the unshielded side. The\ncorresponding turbulent velocity profile indicates the location of mixing\nregions in between the inner and outer streams, outer and shield streams, and\nshield and ambient environment. For all regions up to an X/Deq ~ 5.0 the turbulent velocity on the shielded side (refer to Figure 51) is observed to be\nlower comparedto that on the unshielded side, indicating decreased shear of\nthe nozzle flow due to the presence of shield.\nFurther downstream and up to\nan X/Deq ~ lO.0, the peak mean velocity of the shielded side is noted to be\nhigher than that on the unshielded side due to the slower meanvelocity decay\nrate, indicating a stretching of the jet on the shield side. The dips observed\nin the radial meanvelocity profiles near the nozzle centerline are due to the\nflow separation at the base region of the plug truncation.\nThe laser velocimeter measured static data, presented earlier in Figures\n51 and 52, are comparedin Figures 54 through 56 to the corresponding data\nobtained under simulated flight conditions.\nThis is to demonstrate the effect\nof simulated flight (Vac= 400 ft/s) on the axial variation of meanand turbulent velocities,\nand on the radial variation of meanvelocity.\nBecause of the\nreduction of shear stresses due to the presence of the free-jet,\nthe turbulent\nvelocities measured for X/Deq < i0 during simulated flight are lower than the\ncorresponding static data. This, in general, results in the observed slower\ndecay of the jet plume in simulated flight.\nThe effect of free-jet on the\nflow-field characteristics\nof unsuppressed coannular plug nozzle with partial\nshield is discussed further in Section 5.2.\nThe acoustic data measuredwith the 180\xc2\xb0 shielded unsuppressed coannular\nplug configuration at aerodynamic flow conditions that correspond to the above\nstatic LV data were presented earlier in Section 4.1.3. The measured PNLdirectivity\ndata are repeated in Figure 57 and comparedto the corresponding\nbaseline unsuppressed coannular plug nozzle (TAS-10) data to show the noise\nsuppression due to the partial shield.\nIn addition, the 180\xc2\xb0 shield effectiveness on the directivity\nof the various I/3-octave-band frequencies is presented in Figure 58. The aft quadrant data of this figure indicate increased\nsuppression with increase in frequency. In addition, similar to the shielded\nannular nozzle data of Figures 6 through 8, the fluid shielding results in a\nsignificant attenuation of the high frequency noise for 8i > 130\xc2\xb0. For example, for frequencies > i000 Hz, the maximum\nsuppression at ei = 150\xc2\xb0 is\nobserved to be about 12 dB. The suppression of < 4 dB noted in the front\nquadrant is attributed to modifications in the v_locity gradients by the shield\nflow.\n\n98\n\nORIGINAL\n\nPAGE\n\nOF POOR and\n\nto\n\npredicted\n\nsponding\n\n=\n\nassociated\n\nrespectively\n\nThese\n\ndata\n\nei\n\nei\n\nfrequencies\n\ni/3-octave-bands\n\nrespectively.\nin 2,\n\npeak\n\ncos\n\nspectral\n\nof\nthe\n\nreduction\n\ncontent\n\nat\nthe\nit\n\nhigh\nlaser\nhas\n\nin\n\nconvergent\nof\n\ncirthe\n\nfrequencies\nvelocibeen\n\nshown\n\nin Reference 22 that the supersonic exhaust from the suppressor flow elements\ndecay rapidly to a subsonic flow in all regions downstreamof the plug. This\nis in contrast to the convergent circular nozzle which maintains a supersonic\nflow up to a distance ten times the diameter of the nozzle. The enhancedmixing rate achieved by the increased total surface area of the mechanical suppressor jet leads to the observed rapid decay of the plume, and hence the\nreduction in the sound pressure levels at low and middle frequency ranges.\nThe high frequency noises are from sources in the supersonic flow located on\nthe plug and near the nozzle exit.\nThe perceived noise level directivity\nand selected spectra obtained under\nstatic tests for the typical takeoff, cutback, and approach conditions are presented in Figure 65. The spectral data indicate the significant\nhigh frequency noise that is associated with the suppressor configuration.\nThe spectra\nof the 32-chute suppressor (TAS-6) of the single flow thermal acoustic shield\nstudy (Reference 12) were observed also to have a pronounced high frequency\ncontent.\n4.2.2\nAs\nnozzle\n\nover\n\nusing\na\n\nfor\n\nvelocity\n\nThe\n\n0.56\n\nAt\nfor\n\n0.69\na\n\nfor\n\nTAS-16,\n\nobjective\n\nof\n\nTables\n\nIX\n\nstream\n\nvelocity\n\nconditions.\n\nnozzle\nAs\n\nto\n\nand\n\n-18\n\nof\n\nthe\n\nin\n\nnoise\na\n\nSection\n\nfor\n\nthe\n\n3.1.2,\n\nthe\n\nof\n\nand\n\nwill\n\ninner\n\nbe\n\nrespecidentified\n\npresented\n\nthe\n\nand\n\nand\n\nwere\n\nchosen\n\nthe\nthis\n\nshield\n\nin\n\nsuch\n\nthat\n\n0.6\n\napproximately\n\nover\n\nthe\n\nthe\n\nouter\n\nstream\n\nstream\n\ncondi-\n\ncommunity\n\ninner-to-outer\ntest\n\nstream\n\nrange.\n\norientation\n\nto\n\nThe\n\nthe\n\nvelocity\n\nacoustic\n\nratio\ndata\n\nmicrophones\n\nare\n\ni,o\n\nvr\n\nwas\n\nmeasured\nemployed\n\nwith\nin\n\nstudy.\n\nThe\n\nnormalized\n\nquadrant\n\nangles\n\ndata\n\nperceived\n\nplotted\n\nare\n\nof\n\n0i TM\n\n/aamb)\n\n\xc2\xb0\nPNL\nPlug\n\nSimulated\nNozzle\n\nwith\n\nFlight\n180\n\n\xc2\xb0\n\nData\nand\n\n360\n\nof\n\xc2\xb0\n\nShield.\n\nvelocity\nparameter.\nThe data\nindicate\nthat, for given\nshield\nflow conditions,\nthe normalized\nperceived\nnoise\nlevel data of the full shield\n(0.5 in. thick)\nconfiguration\nare higher\nthan the corresponding\ndata of the 180 \xc2\xb0 shield\n(0.97\nin. thick)\nconfiguration.\nThis is particularly\nexplicit\nfor the static\ntest\ndata.\nAlso,\nthis difference\ndecreases\nwith an increase\nin the mixed\njet\nvelocity.\nAft-quadrant\nstatic\nspectral\ndata at typical\nsented\nin Figure\n82.\nThe data show no significant\nbetween\nthe partial\nand full shield\nconfigurations\n\ntakeoff\nconditions\nare prespectral\ndifferences\ndata up to an aft quadrant\n\nangle\nof e i = 120 \xc2\xb0 . At directivity\nangles\ngreater\nthan 120 \xc2\xb0 , the sound pressure levels\nassociated\nwith the partial\nshielded\nconfiguration\nare lower at\nall frequencies\nthan those of full shielded\nconfigurations.\nRelative\nto the\nunshielded\nbaseline\nsuppressor\nnozzle,\nthe partial\nshield\nconfiguration\nyields\na larger\nsuppression\nat higher\nfrequencies,\nwhile\nthe full shield\nconfiguration yields\na significant\nincrease\nin the low frequency\nspectra.\nCorresponding selected\naft quadrant\nspectra\nobtained\nduring\nsimulated\nflight\ntests are\npresented\nin Figure\n83.\nObservations\nsimilar\nto those of the static\ndata\nare noted;\nhowever,\nno significant\nspectral\ndifferences\nbetween\nthe partial\nand\nfull\n\nshield\n\nconfigurations\n\nare\n\nindicated\n\nup to\n\nei = 130 \xc2\xb0 .\n\nSelected\naft quadrant\nstatic\nand simulated\nflight\nspectral\ndata at typical\ncutback\nconditions\nare presented\nin Figures\n84 and 85, respectively.\nSelected\naft-quadrant\nstatic\nspectra\nat approach\ncondition\nare presented\nin Figure\n86.\nObservations\nsimilar\nto those made earlier\nfor the takeoff\ndata can be applied\nto those\ntest conditions\nalso.\nThe low frequency\nsound pressure\nlevels\nare\nseen to increase.\nTherefore,\nthough\nthe shields\nsignificantly\nsuppressed\nthe\nhigh frequency\nnoise at these angles,\nbecause\nof this increase\nthe overall\nperceived\nnoise\nlevels\nwere not reduced\nby the shields.\nThis is indicated\nby the\ntypical\ntakeoff\nof PNL-directivity\ndata presented\nin Figure\n87.\nThis section\nis concluded\nby comparing\nthe typical\nsound power spectra\nof\nunshielded\nand 360 \xc2\xb0 shielded\nsuppressed\ncoannular\nplug nozzles\nto those of the\nconvergent\ncircular\nnozzle.\nThe static\nspectra\nobtained\nat typical\ntakeoff\nand cutback\nconditions\nare presented\nin Figure\n88.\nThis figure\nshows the\nsignificant\nsound power\nlevel reduction\nobtained\nwith the baseline\nsuppressor\nconfiguration\n(TAS-15)\nrelative\nto the convergent\ncircular\nnozzle\nat all low\nand middle\nfrequencies.\nThis is a result\nof the significantly\nhigher\nmixing\nrate associated\nwith the suppressor\nconfiguration.\nThe increased\nmixing\nrate\nis achieved\nthrough\nan increase\nin surface\narea of the suppressor\njet that is\navailable\nfor shear with the surrounding\nambient\nair.\nHowever,\nno benefit\nis\nnoted\nat high frequencies\nfor sources\nnear the nozzle\nexit.\nIntroducing\nthe\nfull shield\naround\nthe suppressor\nyields\nthe observed\npower level reductions\nin the high frequency\ndata due to shielding\nof the high frequency\nsources\nnear\nthe nozzle\nexit.\nHowever,\nthe presence\nof the shield\nflow decreases\nthe decay\nrate of the suppressor\njet.\nThis leads to the increase\nin the low and middle\nfrequency\npower\nlevels.\nThe mean velocity\ndata that describe\nthe effect\nof\nshield\nflow on the decay rate of the suppressor\njet are presented\nin the PT\n\n_,_\n\ni\n\n.qS\n\n_\n\noOgI\n\ng\nI\n\nI\n\noO\n\n168\n\nI\n\nI\n\nI\n\nI\n\nI\n\n5.0\n\nAEROACOUSTIC\nPREDICTIONS\nTHERMAL\nACOUSTIC\nSHIELDS\n\nFOR\n\nUNSUPPRESSED\n\nCOANNULAR\n\nPLUG\n\nNOZZLE\n\nWITH\n\n5.1\n\nBACKGROUND\n\nsented\n\nIn addition\nto the measured\nacoustic\nand diagnostic\ndata that were\nearlier\nin Section\n4.0, the acoustic\nand flow field distributions\n\nprefor\n\nthe unsuppressed\ncoannular\nplug nozzle,\nwith full and partial\nshields,\nhave been predicted\nduring\nthis study.\nThe modified\nBalsa\n(M*G*B)\nmodel\n(Reference\n32) was used.\n\nfor\n\nThe M*G*B\nassessing\n\ntechnique\nvelocity,\n\nmodel\nis a unified\naerodynamic\nand acoustic\nthe noise characteristics\nof arbitrarily-shaped\n\nuses an extension\ntemperature,\nand\n\nof Reichardt\'s\nmethod\nto predict\nturbulence\nintensity\ndistribution.\n\nthermal\nacoustic\nMani*Gliebe*-\n\nprediction\nnozzles.\n\nmethod\nThe\n\nthe jet plume\nThe turbulent\n\nfluctuations\nproduced\nin the mixing\nregions\nof the jet are assumed\nto be the\nprimary\nsource\nof noise generation,\nas in the classical\ntheories\nof jet noise.\nThe alteration\nof the generated\nnoise by the jet plume\nitself\nas it propagates\nthrough\nthe jet to the far-field\nobserver\n(sound/flow\ninteraction\nor fluid\nshielding)\nis modeled\nLilley\'s\nequation.\n\nusing\n\nthe\n\nhigh-frequency\n\nshielding\n\ntheory\n\nbased\n\non\n\nThese\nbasic modeling\nelements\n(flow field prediction,\nturbulent\nmixing\nnoise\ngeneration,\nand sound/flow\ninteraction)\nhave been linked\ntogether\nin a\ndiscrete\nvolume-element\nformulation.\nThe jet plume\nis divided\ninto elemental\nvolumes,\neach roughly\nthe size of a representative\nturbulence\ncorrelation\nvolume\nappropriate\nto that particular\nlocation\nin the plume.\nEach volume\nelement\nis assigned\nits own characteristic\nfrequency,\nspectrum,\nand acoustic\nintensity.\nThe sound/flow\ninteraction\neffects\nfor each element\nare evaluated\nfrom the flow environment\nof the element.\nThe individual\nvolume\nelements\nare\nassumed\nto be uncorrelated\nto each other,\nso that the total contribution\nto\nthe far-field\nis the sum of the individual\nvolume\nelement\ncontributions.\nAs noted\nearlier,\nthe M*G*B model predicts\nthe flow field and turbulent\nmixing\nnoise\ngeneration\nfor arbitrary\nnozzle\nshapes\nand azimuthally\naverages\nthe flow field and noise source\ncharacteristics\nto predict\nthe far-field\nnoise\ndistribution.\nDuring\nthe single-flow\nstudy of this program\n(Reference\n12), the\nmeasured\nacoustic\nand flow field data of an annular\nplug nozzle\nwith a partial\nshield\nindicated,\nas expected,\nazimuthally\nasymmetric\ncharacteristics.\nHence,\nthe acoustic\nmodeling\nof Reference\n32 was modified\nappropriately\nin Reference\n12 to reflect\nthe asymmetric\nacoustics\nand flow field of the partial\nthermal\nacoustic\nshielded\nconfigurations.\nThe predictions\nwere compared\nin Reference\n12 to the measured\nacoustic\ndata.\nThe chosen predicted\nand measured\ndata comparisons\nindicated\ngood spectral\nagreement\nin the front quadrant\nand similar\ntrends\nin the aft quadrant.\nDuring\nthis investigation,\nthe modified\nM*G*B\nmodel\nin Reference\n12 was used to predict\nthe acoustic\nand flow field characteristics\nof an unsuppressed\ncoannular\nplug nozzle\nwith partial\nand full\nthermal\nacoustic\nshields.\nSelected\ndata-theory\ncomparisons\nof the acoustic\n\n169\n\nand\n\nflow\n\nfield\n\n(mean\n\nand\n\nturbulent\n\nvelocity\n\npresented\nin this section.\nSince mix,\n\nand\n\nturbulent\n\ntend\n\nand\nThe\n\nlowers\n\ncompared\n\nflight\n\nrespectively,\n\nThe\n\n107.\n\nthat:\n\nsimulated\n\nb.\n\nmeasurements\n\nFigure\n\nflow\n\ncase,\n\nindicates\n\na.\n\nin\n\nbe\n\nvelocities\nlower\n\nthan\n\nfor\nthe\n\nthe\n\nflight\n\ncase\n\ncorresponding\n\non\n\nstatic\n\nthe\n\nshield\n\nside\n\nat\n\ncase\n\naxial\n\nall\n\nlocations.\n\nThe\non\n\ncorresponding\nthe\n\nshield\n\n14.7%\nsite\n\nand\n\n15.4%\n\nshield\n\nflight\n\ncase\n\nopposite\n\npredictions\nside\n\nfor\n\nof\n\nside\nthan\n\nshield\n\nV mix\n\nat\nfor\nside\n\nindicate\n\nthe\n\nall\n\nsimulated\n\nand\n\nthe\n\naxial\n\nthe\n\nstatic\n\ndoes\n\nnot\n\nthat\n\nturbulent\nlocations\ncase.\nshow\n\npredicted\n\nflight\n\nany\n\nand\n\npeak\n\nstatic\n\nvelocities\ntend\nThe\n\nto\n\nbe\n\non\n\nthe\n\nlower\n\nmeasured\n\nnoticeable\n\nturbulent\n\ncases\n\nare,\nshield\n\nand\n\nthe\n\nsimulated\n\nfor\n\nturbulent\neffect\n\nof\n\nvelocity\nrespectively,\noppo-\n\nvelocity\nthe\n\non\n\nthe\n\nsimulated\n\nflight.\n\nThe\nwith\n\n184\n\nnext\n\nset\n\nthe\n\nASPL\n\nby\n\nof\nthe\n\ndata-theory\nfull\n\n(360\n\ncomparisons\n\xc2\xb0 ) shield\n\non\n\npresented\nthe\n\nin\n\nunsuppressed\n\nthis\n\nsection\n\ncoannular\n\ndeals\nplug\n\nnozzle (TAS-14) at a typical takeoff cycle for the static condition.\nThe typical aft-quadrant data presented in Figure 108 indicate an acceptable agreement\nbetween the measured and predicted ASPLby the shield.\nThe measured data also\nshow a negligible high frequency noise reduction by the shield at the takeoff\ncycle condition, whereas the predictions showeda modest high frequency noise\nreduction (4 dB at 80 kHz 1/3 octave band). Both the data and the predictions\nindicate low frequency noise amplification by the shield. As in the case of\nthe partial shield on the coannular plug nozzle, the agreementbetween the\nmeasured and predicted ASPLat ei = 90\xc2\xb0 and 60\xc2\xb0 is good at low and high frequencies (see Figures 108b and i08c).\nSince the acoustic benefit of the shield is mainly in the aft quadrant\nfor the unsuppressed coannular plug nozzle, this section is concluded with\ndata-theory comparisons in the aft quadrant only for typical approach and cutback conditions.\nFigures 109 and ii0 show comparisons of static ASPL the full shield\nby\non the unsuppressed coannular plug nozzle at ei = 130\xc2\xb0 for approach and cutback conditions, respectively.\nThe figures show that the predicted trends\nagree with the data. It should be noted that suppression levels predicted\nand measured at the approach and cutback cycle conditions are higher than those\nindicated earlier at the takeoff cycle. In addition, both the predictions and\ndata indicate that the peak level of suppression due to the full shield at\napproach and cutback cycles is about the same. However, the high frequency\nnoise reduction potential of the shield is less at high outer and inner jet\nvelocities.\nA similar observation was madein Reference 12 in the context of\nthe single flow primary nozzles with the thermal acoustic shield.\nThus, the\nM*G*Bprediction model has been shown to predict correCt trends of spectral\nsuppression characteristics\nof the shield on an unsuppressed coannular plug\nnozzle at various cycle conditions.\nThe principal\n\nconclusions of this study are:\n\nThe overall trends in the flow field characteristics\nof an unsuppressed coannular plug nozzle with partial shield that were predicted by the modified M*G*Bmodel are in reasonable agreement with\nthe corresponding trends in the LV measureddata.\nBoth the predicted and measured flow field characteristics\nconfirm\nthat the principal reason for the observed amplification of the low\nfrequency noise is the elongation of the jet plume by the shield.\nThe predicted suppression of high frequency noise by the shield in\nthe aft quadrant is higher than the measurements; but both the data\nand predictions showsimilar trends in the suppression spectra.\nBoth the predictions and measurementsof the noise suppression by\nthe shield in the aft quadrant indicate that the shield yields\nappreciable noise reductions at low and middle engine power settings\n(approach and cutback, respectively) and that its potential to\nreduce noise at the high power setting (takeoff) decreases.\n185\n\nO_ POOR\nllAl_\n\nQ,UALIT_\n\nllO.\n16\n\n17\n\ni\n\n18\n\n19\n\n\'\n\n20\n\n21\n\n22\n\n2\'_\n\n24\n\n25\n\n26\n\n2"7\n\n2tl\n\n29\n\n_10\n\n31\n\n32\n\n33\n\n34\n\n_\n\n_16\n\n37\n\n38\n\n_J)\n\ndlO\n\ndl\n\n,"-4\nI\n<\nI.I-I\n\no\n\n3O\n\n,-4\nill\n>\nli)\n\n;\n\nI\n\n_\n\nJ\n\nJ\n\n..\n\n\xc2\xa2J\n\n_\n\nt\n\ni\n\n1\n\n!\n\n!\n\nI\n\n2O\nlD\n\n\',\n\n:\n\',\n\'\n\nC\no\n\ni0\n\n_,\n\nI\'_\n\n!\n\ni\n\n_ I t\n\nt\n\n\'_ i\n\nI\n\ni\n\nI\n\nl\n\nI\n\nI\n\n*\n\n0\n\n\'-_\n\nI ) _\n\nJ.-i\'-,xo\n_---_\nT\ni\ni -\n\n:\ni\n\n4\n\nz_ _\nI_,,\nI\n\nm\n\no\n\n!\n\n,\n-i0\n\n__\n\ni\n\n,\n\n\'\n\nI\n\n,\n\ni\n\ni\n\n!\n\ni\n\nI\ni\n\nI\nI\n\n!\n\n_\n\n!\n\n_\n\n,\n\nI\n\ni\n\nI\n\n\'\n\nt\n:\n]\n\nI\n\nt\n\n_\n\n_ ,\n\n\'\n\nJ\n\n_\n\n!\n\nI ! _ ! Abstract\n\nThe influences\nof selected\ngeometric and aerodynamic flow variables\nof an unsuppressed coannular\nplug nozzle and a coannular\nplug nozzle with a 20-chute outer\nstream suppressor\nwere experimentally\ndetermined.\nA total\nof 136 static\nand\nsimulated\nflight\nacoustic\ntest points were conducted with 9 scale-model\nnozzles.\nAlso,\naerodynamic measurements of four selected\nplumes were made with a laser\nvelocimeter.\nThe presence of the 180\xc2\xb0 shield\nproduced different\nmixing characteristics\non the shield side compared to the unshield side because of the reduced\nmixing with ambient air on the shielded side. This resulted in a stretching of\nthe jet, yielding a higher peak mean velocity up to a length of lO equivalent\ndiameters from the nozzle exit. The 180\xc2\xb0 shield in community orientation around\nthe suppressed coannular plug nozzle yielded acoustic benefit at all observer\nangles for a simulated takeoff. While the effect of shield-to-outer stream\nvelocity ratio was small at angles up to 120\xc2\xb0, beyond this angle significant\nacoustic benefit was realized with a shield-to-outer stream velocity ratio of\n0.64. While the reduction in the aft quadrant by shielding was noted only at\nvery high frequencies, significant noise suppressions at middle and high frequencies were achieved at all angles because of changes in the flow fields and\nsource alterations produced by the shield flow. However, as a result of stretching of the jet on the shield side, low frequency jet noise was greater than for\nthe unshielded configuration.\n17\n\nKey Words\n\n(Suggested\n\n18.
